# CODEX RECOVERY AND INTEGRATION PROMPT

## User
**Timestamp:** 2026-07-19T00:16:01.766Z

CODEX RECOVERY AND INTEGRATION PROMPT

Consolidate Vision Waypoint Phases B-1 Through B-6 Into One Canonical Application

You are performing a complete recovery, audit, reconciliation, and integration of the Vision Waypoint Phase B implementation.

The implementation appears to have been developed across multiple separate Git worktrees or cloned working directories:

Codex_TreasureHunt
Codex_TreasureHunt-phaseb2
Codex_TreasureHunt-phaseb3
Codex_TreasureHunt-phaseb4
Codex_TreasureHunt-phaseb5
Codex_TreasureHunt-phaseb6

These phase directories were intended to support parallel work, not to become permanently separate applications.

The final required result is:

One canonical repository
One integrated codebase
One coherent database migration history
One shared set of domain contracts
One shared Player interface
One shared Captain interface
One shared Studio interface
One canonical development server
One canonical port: 3000

Do not blindly copy files from one phase directory into another.

Do not assume that a Codex chat reporting completion means its work was merged.

Do not assume GitHub main contains all completed Phase B work.

Do not delete any worktree, clone, folder, branch, commit, migration, untracked file, or local change until the complete recovery and integration has been reviewed.

⸻

1. Primary Mission

Recover and integrate all legitimate work from Vision Waypoint Phases B-1 through B-6 into one canonical integration branch.

You must:

1. Identify the exact repository/worktree arrangement.
2. Preserve every phase implementation.
3. Determine what each phase actually completed.
4. Identify all branches, commits, uncommitted changes, and generated artifacts.
5. Compare each phase against its original governing prompt.
6. Reconcile overlapping source changes.
7. Consolidate database migrations.
8. Consolidate domain and protocol contracts.
9. Port phase functionality into the current canonical UI.
10. Run focused validation after each phase is integrated.
11. Run complete validation after all phases are combined.
12. Publish the integration branch safely.
13. Produce a detailed integration and recovery report.
14. Stop for review before merging into main.
15. Preserve all phase worktrees until final approval.

This is both:

* a repository recovery task;
* and a full software integration task.

It is not merely a Git merge exercise.

⸻

2. Governing Source-of-Truth Order

Before modifying source, locate and read all applicable governing material.

The governing order is:

1. TT-VISION-GOV-001
   Vision Waypoint and External AR Governing Specification
2. TT-VISION-PHASE-B-001
   Phase B Implementation Roadmap
3. Original prompts for Phases B-1 through B-6
4. Phase-specific ADRs and implementation records
5. Existing project-wide architecture and design documentation
6. Current canonical repository conventions
7. This recovery and integration prompt

Expected locations may include:

Development_Docs/
Development_Docs/AR/
Development_Docs/AR/ADRs/
Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B1/
Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B2/
Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B3/
Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B4/
Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B5/
Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B6/
Codex_Chats/

Search thoroughly.

Do not invent replacement architecture merely because phase implementations disagree.

When two implementations conflict, use the governing documents and semantic dependency order to determine the correct combined design.

Record any material decision in an ADR or integration decision log.

⸻

3. Non-Negotiable Safety Rules

Before changing anything:

1. Identify the canonical repository path.
2. Identify every Codex_TreasureHunt-phaseb* directory.
3. Determine whether each directory is:
    * a linked Git worktree;
    * a separate full clone;
    * a copied folder;
    * a detached worktree;
    * a generated build output;
    * or another arrangement.
4. Record the exact state of every directory.
5. Preserve all staged changes.
6. Preserve all unstaged changes.
7. Preserve all untracked files.
8. Preserve all local branches.
9. Preserve all stashes.
10. Preserve all phase-specific commits.
11. Preserve all migration files.
12. Preserve all phase documentation and completion reports.

Never use:

git reset --hard
git clean
git checkout -- .
git restore .
git restore --staged .
git stash --all
force push
broad file-copy replacement
automatic conflict resolution using only ours
automatic conflict resolution using only theirs

Do not delete or remove any worktree.

Do not run cleanup tools against the phase folders.

Do not allow generated dependency folders such as node_modules, .next, build output, caches, or temporary databases to influence source integration.

Do not stage unrelated files using broad commands such as:

git add .
git add -A

Stage intentionally by path.

⸻

4. Canonical Recovery Branch

Perform the recovery from the canonical Codex_TreasureHunt repository.

Create a dedicated integration branch, for example:

integration/vision-waypoint-b1-b6

The integration branch must be based on the correct current canonical branch.

Before creating it, record:

* canonical branch;
* canonical HEAD;
* upstream;
* ahead/behind status;
* remote HEAD;
* worktree status;
* untracked files;
* active development server;
* current database configuration;
* current port usage.

Do not modify main directly.

Do not merge the integration branch into main automatically.

Push the integration branch after successful checkpoints and final validation.

⸻

5. Complete Worktree and Clone Inventory

From the canonical repository, run and record:

git worktree list --porcelain
git branch --all --verbose
git log --all --graph --decorate --oneline
git remote -v
git status --short --branch
git stash list

Inside every Phase B directory, run:

git rev-parse --show-toplevel
git rev-parse --git-common-dir
git rev-parse --git-dir
git branch --show-current
git rev-parse HEAD
git rev-parse --abbrev-ref --symbolic-full-name @{upstream}
git status --short --branch
git remote -v
git stash list
git log --oneline --decorate --max-count=30
git merge-base HEAD main

If an upstream does not exist, record that fact without treating it as failure.

For every directory, record:

Absolute path
Repository identity
Worktree or clone
Branch
HEAD commit
Base commit
Remote
Upstream
Ahead/behind state
Staged files
Unstaged files
Untracked files
Stashes
Relevant commits
Build artifacts
Database files
Environment files
Last modified time

Create:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B_Worktree_Inventory.md

⸻

6. Preserve Uncommitted Phase Work

If any phase folder contains uncommitted source changes:

1. Inspect every changed file.
2. Separate source from generated output.
3. Do not commit:
    * node_modules;
    * .next;
    * build output;
    * logs;
    * temporary database copies;
    * local secrets;
    * caches.
4. Create a preservation branch specific to that phase if needed.
5. Commit legitimate uncommitted source with a clearly labeled recovery commit.

Example:

recovery/phase-b4-uncommitted

Example commit:

recovery(vision): preserve uncommitted phase B-4 work

Do not alter the intent of the work during preservation.

The initial goal is to ensure that no source exists only as an uncommitted local file.

⸻

7. Recover Separate Clone History

If any phase directory is a separate clone rather than a shared worktree:

1. Verify that it points to the same repository origin.
2. Identify its unique branch and commits.
3. Add it temporarily as a local recovery remote if necessary.
4. Fetch the relevant branch and commit history into the canonical repository.
5. Preserve exact commit identities where practical.
6. Do not push unrelated local branches.
7. Do not overwrite an existing branch with a different history.

Example temporary remote names:

phaseb2-recovery
phaseb3-recovery
phaseb4-recovery
phaseb5-recovery
phaseb6-recovery

After fetching, verify that every unique source commit can be addressed from the canonical repository.

Document the recovery method.

⸻

8. Phase Provenance and Completeness Audit

Create a full provenance matrix for B-1 through B-6.

For each phase, identify:

* original prompt;
* governing requirements;
* source folder;
* source branch;
* starting commit;
* ending commit;
* merge base;
* unique commit range;
* changed source files;
* deleted files;
* migration files;
* schema changes;
* dependencies added;
* environment variables added;
* API routes added;
* domain types added;
* protocol types added;
* frontend components added;
* native/desktop files added;
* PWA files added;
* tests added;
* documentation added;
* implementation record;
* completion report;
* test results claimed;
* test results reproducible;
* uncommitted work;
* pushed state;
* merged state;
* conflicts with other phases;
* stale-base risks;
* placeholder or mock status;
* actual completion percentage.

Create:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B1_B6_Provenance_Matrix.md
  Phase_B1_B6_Changed_Files.csv
  Phase_B1_B6_Test_Evidence.md
  Phase_B1_B6_Completion_Assessment.md

Do not classify a phase as complete based only on:

* chat completion;
* documentation;
* scaffolding;
* placeholder interfaces;
* a passing typecheck;
* mock-only behavior where production behavior was required;
* isolated build success.

Use source and test evidence.

⸻

9. Dependency Analysis

Determine the actual logical dependencies among B-1 through B-6.

The default expectation is:

B-1
Shared platform, domain, versioning, protocol, adapters
B-2
Capture companion and acquisition infrastructure
B-3
Vision build, package, inference, and verification pipeline
B-4
Studio authoring, reference collection, calibration, testing
B-5
Player and Captain runtime integration
B-6
Production hardening, rollout, observability, certification

Do not assume all phases were implemented from the output of the prior phase.

Check each phase’s merge base.

If B-3, B-4, B-5, or B-6 were all created directly from B-1, integration must explicitly combine their independent changes.

Create:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B_Dependency_Graph.md

Identify:

* hard dependencies;
* soft dependencies;
* overlapping files;
* overlapping migrations;
* overlapping contracts;
* ordering constraints;
* required adaptation work.

⸻

10. Integration Plan Before Code Changes

Before merging or cherry-picking any implementation commit, create:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B1_B6_Integration_Plan.md

The plan must define:

1. Integration order.
2. Branches or commit ranges to incorporate.
3. Commits to exclude.
4. Reasons for exclusions.
5. Shared files likely to conflict.
6. Database migration strategy.
7. Contract consolidation strategy.
8. UI adaptation strategy.
9. Test sequence.
10. Rollback checkpoints.
11. Validation ownership.
12. Port and server isolation.
13. Database isolation.
14. Final publication plan.

Do not begin broad integration until this plan exists.

⸻

11. Commit Selection Rules

For each phase, classify commits into:

APPLICATION_SOURCE
DATABASE_MIGRATION
TESTS
DOCUMENTATION
CHAT_SYNC
GENERATED_OUTPUT
ENVIRONMENT_ONLY
RECOVERY
UNRELATED

Integrate:

* application source;
* legitimate migrations;
* tests;
* relevant documentation;
* relevant recovery commits.

Usually exclude or separately handle:

* chat synchronization commits;
* generated build artifacts;
* local environment files;
* dependency caches;
* unrelated product work;
* duplicate documentation synchronization.

Do not cherry-pick chat-sync commits merely because they are adjacent to application commits.

Do not lose phase implementation work hidden inside mixed commits. If a mixed commit contains both application source and unrelated changes, extract the relevant patch carefully and document it.

⸻

12. Controlled Phase Integration

Integrate each phase in the dependency order determined by the roadmap and audit.

The expected checkpoint sequence is:

integration(vision): incorporate phase B-1 foundation
integration(vision): incorporate phase B-2 capture infrastructure
integration(vision): incorporate phase B-3 vision pipeline
integration(vision): incorporate phase B-4 studio tooling
integration(vision): incorporate phase B-5 runtime experience
integration(vision): incorporate phase B-6 hardening

After each phase:

1. Resolve conflicts semantically.
2. Run formatting on changed files.
3. Run focused typecheck.
4. Run focused unit tests.
5. Run focused schema tests.
6. Run focused integration tests.
7. Record failures and fixes.
8. Create a checkpoint commit.
9. Push the integration branch.
10. Continue only when the current checkpoint is coherent.

Do not wait until all phases are merged before discovering that B-2 broke B-1’s contracts.

⸻

13. Conflict Resolution Rules

Never resolve a conflict using blanket “ours” or “theirs.”

For each conflict:

1. Identify which phase introduced each side.
2. Identify the governing requirement.
3. Identify newer canonical improvements on main.
4. Determine whether both sides contain valid behavior.
5. Build the combined implementation.
6. Add or update tests proving the resolution.
7. Record the decision.

Maintain:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B_Conflict_Resolution_Log.md

For every conflict record:

File
Phases involved
Original intent
Conflict cause
Chosen behavior
Code retained from each side
Tests added
Remaining limitation

⸻

14. Protect Current Canonical UI Work

The current canonical branch may contain newer:

* navigation;
* unified shell;
* color system;
* responsive behavior;
* Tall Tale journal UI;
* accessibility improvements;
* animation changes;
* Player Library changes;
* Captain Library changes;
* Studio changes.

Do not restore stale phase-specific UI wholesale.

Where a phase branch contains functionality but older presentation code:

1. Extract the functional behavior.
2. Port it into the current canonical component structure.
3. Use the current design system.
4. Preserve current navigation.
5. Preserve current color/theme behavior.
6. Preserve current responsive layout.
7. Preserve current accessibility behavior.
8. Preserve canonical journal usage.

The final product must not feel like six different applications taped together at the edges.

⸻

Create one authoritative implementation for each shared contract.

Explicitly audit and reconcile:

* VisionWaypoint;

* feature flags;
* capability detection;
* platform adapters;
* desktop bridge;
* PWA bridge;
* protocol errors;
* telemetry;
* audit records.

There must not be phase-local duplicate versions of these contracts after integration.

Use schema validation at trust boundaries.

Preserve backwards compatibility where required.

Document any schema version bump.

⸻

16. Database and Migration Reconciliation

Database integration must remain serialized.

Create:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B_Migration_Ledger.md

For every migration record:

* phase;
* filename;
* parent schema state;
* models added;
* fields added;
* fields changed;
* indexes;
* unique constraints;
* foreign keys;
* data migrations;
* rollback implications;
* whether it was applied anywhere;
* conflict with another phase.

Identify whether phases created migrations independently from the same schema baseline.

Do not simply sort conflicting migrations by timestamp.

The final migration history must support:

1. Clean database bootstrap.
2. Upgrade from the canonical pre-B schema.
3. Upgrade from B-1-only schema.
4. Seeded development database.
5. Test database creation.
6. ORM client generation.
7. Rollback or recovery documentation.

Preserve published-version immutability.

Preserve idempotency constraints.

Preserve exact-once story progression.

Preserve referential integrity.

If necessary, create a new integration migration that reconciles independent phase changes.

Do not edit already-applied production migrations unless absolutely necessary and documented.

⸻

17. Exactly-Once and Concurrency Verification

The combined system must prove:

* repeated verification submissions do not create duplicate accepted events;
* repeated processing does not advance the story twice;
* reused idempotency keys with altered payloads are rejected;
* stale verification results cannot advance a later story block;
* Captain fallback cannot double-complete an objective;
* automatic verification and Captain confirmation cannot both advance the story;
* retries are distinguishable from duplicates;
* session concurrency is enforced;
* publication cannot mutate an existing published waypoint version.

Use database transactions for multi-step state changes.

Unique constraints alone are not sufficient proof.

⸻

18. Front-End Integration Requirements

The final integrated application must use one shared frontend.

Studio

Integrate:

* waypoint library;
* create waypoint;
* edit draft;
* version history;
* reference collection;
* build status;
* calibration;
* test workflow;
* publication;
* immutable-version display;
* story binding;
* compatibility status;
* error recovery.

Player

Integrate:

* waypoint objective;
* Inspect Surroundings;
* permission state;
* capture state;
* verification progress;
* matched;
* not matched;
* low confidence;
* retry;
* timeout;
* offline;
* unavailable capability;
* Captain fallback;
* accessible status announcements;
* deterministic final story state.

Captain

Integrate:

* active verification requests;
* attempt history;
* safe evidence summary;
* accept;
* reject;
* request retry;
* fallback resolution;
* audit history;
* stale-request behavior.

Shared

Preserve:

* canonical navigation;
* current design system;
* current theme;
* responsive behavior;
* accessibility;
* motion preferences;
* role boundaries;
* Player-safe data projection.

⸻

19. Desktop and PWA Consolidation

The final system must not contain separate duplicated applications for:

* browser;
* PWA;
* Windows desktop.

The shared frontend must remain canonical.

Platform differences must exist behind adapters.

Audit:

* PWA manifest;
* service worker;
* cache boundaries;
* offline behavior;
* desktop shell;
* desktop bridge;
* capability detection;
* capture adapter;
* filesystem adapter;
* update behavior;
* protocol pairing;
* local service communication.

Do not cache private mutable API responses.

Do not store secrets in desktop source.

Do not permit silent capture.

Do not create a second desktop-only story engine.

⸻

20. Feature Flag Consolidation

Create one authoritative feature-flag system.

At minimum reconcile:

visionWaypoints.enabled
visionWaypoints.studio.enabled
visionWaypoints.player.enabled
visionWaypoints.mockVerifier.enabled
visionWaypoints.capture.enabled
visionWaypoints.buildPipeline.enabled
visionWaypoints.externalProvider.enabled
visionWaypoints.captainFallback.enabled
visionWaypoints.pwa.enabled
visionWaypoints.desktop.enabled

Feature flags and runtime capabilities must remain separate.

The UI must resolve:

feature enabled
platform supported
permission available
provider available
package compatible
offline capable
fallback available

Do not expose controls that cannot function.

⸻

21. Security and Privacy Review

Perform a focused security review covering:

* raw frame handling;
* screenshot handling;
* evidence retention;
* pairing tokens;
* provider authentication;
* request replay;
* session binding;
* waypoint-version binding;
* package hash validation;
* unsupported schema versions;
* unsafe external input;
* API authorization;
* Captain permissions;
* Studio publication permissions;
* local desktop bridge exposure;
* service-worker caching;
* logging of private story data.

Do not store raw image data in generic JSON fields.

Do not expose unpublished waypoint data to Players.

Do not allow a provider result to claim Captain authority.

Do not silently capture frames.

Record findings in:

Development_Docs/AR/Phase_B_Integration/
  Phase_B_Security_Privacy_Review.md

⸻

22. Test and Validation Environment Isolation

Before mutating tests:

1. Identify the canonical database.
2. Create a unique isolated test database or copy.
3. Use an explicit absolute database connection.
4. Record the database identity.
5. Record the development server PID.
6. Record the validation port.
7. Verify the application is connected to the isolated database.
8. Preserve the canonical database hash, size, and modification time.
9. Run mutations only against the isolated test database.
10. Verify the canonical database remains unchanged.

Do not run integration tests against a shared local development database.

Do not use port 3000 for temporary validation if the existing canonical server already owns it.

Temporary isolated ports are allowed during integration.

The final canonical application must run on port 3000.

⸻

23. Required Focused Tests

After integrating each phase, run the relevant focused tests.

The final integrated suite must include:

Domain

* waypoint creation;
* draft version creation;
* immutable publication;
* new draft from published version;
* lifecycle transition validation;
* compatibility validation;
* story binding to exact version.

Protocol

* valid request;
* invalid schema;
* unsupported schema;
* wrong waypoint version;
* wrong package hash;
* wrong session;
* expired request;
* duplicate event;
* altered duplicate payload;
* invalid confidence;
* invalid provider authority.

Story engine

* successful verification completes once;
* failed verification does not complete;
* retry succeeds;
* duplicate success does not duplicate progression;
* stale success does not progress;
* Captain confirmation completes once;
* automatic and Captain paths cannot both complete;
* refresh does not repeat completion.

Studio

* create;
* edit;
* publish;
* clone version;
* bind;
* preview;
* calibration failure;
* incompatible package;
* validation errors.

Player

* ready;
* requesting;
* capturing;
* verifying;
* success;
* failure;
* retry;
* timeout;
* offline;
* unsupported;
* Captain fallback;
* keyboard;
* screen reader;
* reduced motion.

Captain

* request list;
* detail;
* approve;
* reject;
* retry request;
* stale request;
* duplicate decision;
* audit history.

PWA and desktop

* capability resolution;
* adapter selection;
* unsupported fallback;
* offline shell;
* safe caching;
* desktop bridge validation;
* no duplicate frontend implementation.

⸻

24. Required End-to-End Proof

Run a complete isolated end-to-end workflow:

Studio creates waypoint
        ↓
Draft version is persisted
        ↓
Reference data is attached or mocked as allowed
        ↓
Build/test process runs
        ↓
Immutable version is published
        ↓
Story block binds exact published version
        ↓
Story is published
        ↓
Playthrough starts
        ↓
Player reaches waypoint objective
        ↓
Inspect Surroundings is invoked
        ↓
Correct platform adapter runs
        ↓
Verification request is persisted
        ↓
Verification result is validated
        ↓
Story advances exactly once
        ↓
Browser refresh occurs
        ↓
Story remains advanced once
        ↓
Duplicate result is submitted
        ↓
No duplicate progression occurs

Also prove:

Failure
Retry
Timeout
Stale result
Captain confirmation
Unsupported capability
Offline behavior
Package incompatibility

Record exact requests, events, database rows, and terminal states without exposing secrets.

⸻

25. Runtime and Port Consolidation

At the end of integration:

* one canonical source tree must contain all Phase B functionality;
* one canonical development command must start the app;
* one canonical environment must be documented;
* one canonical database configuration must be used;
* one canonical development server must run on port 3000.

Do not leave phase-specific builds presented as separate product versions.

Phase worktrees may remain for safety, but they must not be required to run the application.

Document which old ports were used temporarily and confirm they are not part of the final workflow.

⸻

26. Final Repository Validation

Run repository-supported commands, including appropriate equivalents of:

npm run format:check
npm run lint
npm run typecheck
npm test
npm run assets:validate
npm run build
npm run validate

Also run:

* database migration validation;
* clean bootstrap;
* seeded bootstrap;
* protocol compatibility tests;
* focused Phase B E2E;
* PWA build validation;
* desktop build validation where supported.

Do not run multiple full validation suites concurrently against the same build directory or database.

Classify every result as:

PASS
FAIL
SKIPPED
BLOCKED
ENVIRONMENTAL
BASELINE FAILURE
TASK REGRESSION

A skipped test is not a pass.

⸻

Final state

⸻

28. GitHub Publication

Push the integration branch to GitHub.

Open a draft pull request targeting main.

The draft PR must include:

* phase provenance summary;
* integration sequence;
* migration notes;
* conflict summary;
* validation summary;
* known limitations;
* worktrees preserved;
* explicit statement that the PR is not yet merged.

Do not merge the PR automatically.

Do not delete source branches automatically.

Do not remove worktrees automatically.

Stop for human review after the integration branch and report are complete.

⸻

29. Completion Gate

Do not declare this task complete unless all of the following are true:

1. Every phase directory has been inventoried.
2. Every phase branch and commit is accounted for.
3. Every uncommitted source change has been preserved.
4. Every phase has been assessed against its original prompt.
5. All valid Phase B source exists in one integration branch.
6. No entire phase folder was copied blindly over another.
7. Shared contracts have one authoritative implementation.
8. Database migrations form one valid sequence.
9. Published waypoint versions remain immutable.
10. Story progression remains exactly-once.
11. Stale results cannot progress the story.
12. Player, Captain, and Studio use one shared application.
13. Browser, PWA, and desktop use shared frontend source.
14. The current canonical UI and navigation are preserved.
15. Focused tests pass or failures are documented.
16. Full validation passes or blockers are documented.
17. The integrated application runs from the canonical repository.
18. The canonical application runs on port 3000.
19. The integration branch is pushed.
20. A draft PR is created.
21. The final report is complete.
22. Old phase folders and worktrees remain preserved.
23. Nothing has been merged to main without review.

Recover the work, integrate it carefully, validate it thoroughly, publish the integration branch, create the draft PR, and stop for review.

A failed lane returns partial evidence and a precise blocker. The coordinator discloses any gap that remains material to completion.\n\n### 23. Final verification\n\nBefore claiming completion:\n\n- re-read the original user request and governing sources;\n- map every acceptance criterion to a delivered change or verified result;\n- reconcile every lane output and resolve or disclose contradictions;\n- confirm no material agent result remains unreviewed;\n- inspect the complete integrated diff and working tree for accidental scope expansion;\n- verify shared-file ownership and handoffs are complete;\n- run required focused, integrated, runtime, regression, accessibility, performance, security, migration, build, or acceptance checks as applicable;\n- distinguish skipped, unverified, pre-existing, and failed checks;\n- confirm generated artifacts and unrelated work were not accidentally staged or treated as source; and\n- run the single coordinator-owned repository finalization gate from `AGENTS.md`.\n\nFor documentation-only work, use proportionate document validation and do not launch the application or full test suite unless a governing instruction explicitly requires it.\n\n### 24. Final report format\n\nThe coordinator reports:\n\n```text\nOutcome: what was completed\nParallel execution: lanes, modes, ownership boundaries, waves, maximum concurrency, and why the decomposition was safe/useful\nSubagent lifecycle: total unique workers; important results; failed, blocked, replaced, or cancelled lanes; and reconciliation/integration status\nParallel execution outcome for substantial tasks: effect on throughput, capacity, depth/coverage, verification, elapsed time, duplication/overhead, and improvements for the next decomposition\nAffected files/systems: task-authored changes, sync-owned changes, and pre-existing work classified separately\nValidation: commands/checks, exit status, and material evidence\nFailures/limitations: unresolved or skipped checks and why\nRemaining risks: known risks that remain within or outside scope\nFollow-up: only work genuinely outside the requested scope\nChat archive: required synchronization result\nDevelopment docs: required synchronization result\n```\n\nFor every substantial task that used subagents, include the complete final parallel-execution summary required by the communication plan: total unique subagents, maximum simultaneous workers, waves, roles and ownership boundaries, read-only and write-enabled lanes, important results from each lane, failures/blocks/replacements/cancellations, reconciliation, realized capacity/depth/coverage/verification/time benefits, avoidable duplication or overhead, and decomposition improvements. Keep the assessment concise and evidence-based. Do not claim speculative numerical percentages unless timing or work data was actually recorded.\n\nFor every substantial task, the final execution assessment must also state concisely and from observed task evidence:\n\n- whether independent work began promptly;\n- whether useful capacity remained unnecessarily idle;\n- whether critical-path work received priority;\n- whether completed results were reviewed and integrated promptly;\n- whether parallelization materially reduced elapsed time;\n- what avoidable waiting, duplication, or planning overhead occurred; and\n- how a similar future task could finish faster.\n\nDo not invent timing figures, duration estimates, or percentages that were not measured.\n\nThe report provides concise rationale, evidence, decisions, and results. It does not expose private chain-of-thought or paste raw agent logs.\n\n## Standard parallel workflow patterns\n\nAdapt these patterns to the task rather than copying them mechanically.\n\n### Repository-wide audit\n\nTypical lanes include repository/architecture census, one or more subsystem reviews, runtime behavior, performance, accessibility, security, testing, data integrity, documentation consistency, missing opportunities, evidence verification, and final reconciliation. Target six to twelve workers when that many real categories exist. Preserve the audit prompt, taxonomy, severity definitions, evidence rules, and report format; give each lane a bounded evidence surface; verify severe/disputed findings; and centralize deduplication, severity reconciliation, and the final coherent audit.\n\n### Multi-feature implementation\n\n1. Establish shared architecture/contracts and identify shared files.\n2. Place genuinely independent feature lanes in separate worktrees or assign disjoint paths.\n3. Give shared architecture, schemas, configuration, manifests, and lockfiles one owner.\n4. Let each feature lane run focused tests.\n5. Integrate in dependency order under one owner.\n6. Run final full-system verification once on the combined state.\n\n### Bug investigation\n\nPotential lanes include independent reproduction, static code tracing, runtime tracing, regression history, test-gap analysis, platform-specific behavior, dependency behavior, and alternative-hypothesis verification. Keep hypotheses distinct and evidence-backed. The coordinator reconciles them and selects a supported root cause before authorizing implementation. Parallel fixes for the same suspected defect are normally redundant unless intentionally comparing isolated approaches.\n\n### Refactor\n\nStart architecture mapping, consumer inventory, and test-baseline lanes in parallel. Serialize shared-interface changes under one owner, then fan out independent package/component migrations with disjoint ownership. Integrate in dependency order and run compatibility/regression verification after all consumers move.\n\n### Frontend experience work\n\nPotential lanes include route/shell structure, navigation, bounded component groups, animation/interaction, design-system consistency, responsive behavior, accessibility, performance, browser reproduction, test coverage, visual verification, and integration review. Use up to twelve when these are genuinely independent. Assign one owner to root layout, providers, shared tokens/global styles, and route shells, plus one runtime/browser owner. Finish with an integrated responsive, keyboard, motion-mode, console, performance, and UX review against the original acceptance criteria.\n\n### Backend or database work\n\nPotential lanes include API, services, repositories, schema analysis, data integrity, security, tests, operational readiness, observability, and documentation. Separate them only where evidence or files do not overlap. Give schemas and the ordered migration chain one authoritative writer and one database/migration operator. Serialize migration generation/application and shared state mutation. Integrate API/service contracts before final database, security, regression, and deployment-readiness validation.\n\n### Documentation task\n\nPotential lanes include source inventory, contradiction review, terminology, factual verification, structural review, instruction-discovery validation, configuration validation, and editorial integration. Fan out read-only discovery and fact-checking by topic. Topic-specific drafting may run in parallel only with disjoint document ownership. Use one editorial integration owner for shared documents, terminology, links, and final formatting. Verify claims against sources and run proportionate diff/format/link checks. Do not create extra helper documents when the requested output is fixed.\n\n### Homogeneous batch investigations\n\nWhen the installed client exposes `spawn_agents_on_csv` or a verified equivalent, optional batch fan-out may handle many independent items with the same analysis: one component, route, package, animation system, test failure, migration target, document, or incident per row. Treat this capability as client-surface dependent and experimental; use ordinary named lanes when clearer.\n\nEach batch requires a stable item ID, explicit input columns, fixed output schema, scope and non-scope, evidence fields, confidence, exactly one result per worker, bounded runtime, maximum safe concurrency, consolidated output, coordinator reconciliation, and retained error rows. Never silently drop failures or assume a batch tool exists without verifying the current client.\n\n## Anti-patterns\n\nDo not:\n\n- process independent areas sequentially without a concrete reason;\n- leave useful worker slots idle while ready meaningful work exists;\n- wait for an entire worker wave when one slot becomes available;\n- wait for every discovery lane before starting implementation that has sufficient verified inputs;\n- wait for every implementation lane before integrating completed independent work when incremental integration is safe;\n- require every worker to finish before reviewing completed high-priority output;\n- spawn agents with substantially identical scopes;\n- make every agent scan the entire repository;\n- make every worker rediscover repository partial evidence;\n2. update dependency edges, ownership, locks, status, risk, and validation;\n3. notify affected lanes and stop conflicting writers before reassignment;\n4. record the material discovery or decision;\n5. start newly ready independent work promptly;\n6. review and integrate completed high-priority output without waiting for unrelated lanes; and\n7. avoid unnecessary restarts.\n\nThe plan serves the task. Subagent communication plan\r\n\r\nSubagent use must never be invisible to the user. Every Tier 1 or Tier 2 plan that uses workers must include a communication plan covering the items below. If a Tier 0 task uses a distinct verification or other worker, the same launch and lifecycle disclosures apply even though the full planning template does not. These rules apply to one worker, multiple specialists, full-capacity fan-out, later waves, replacements, verification lanes, read-only or write lanes, test lanes, and batch workers.\r\n\r\n#### Initial manifest format and launch timing\r\n\r\nBefore or immediately after launching workers, provide a visible chat update titled `Subagent started`, `Subagents started`, or an equally clear wave-specific title. Preserve the audit prompt, taxonomy, severity definitions, evidence rules, and report format; give each lane a bounded evidence surface; verify severe/disputed findings; and centralize deduplication, severity reconciliation, and the final coherent audit.\r\n\r\n### Multi-feature implementation\r\n\r\n1. Establish shared architecture/contracts and identify shared files.\r\n2. Place genuinely independent feature lanes in separate worktrees or assign disjoint paths.\r\n3. Give shared architecture, schemas, configuration, manifests, and lockfiles one owner.\r\n4. Let each feature lane run focused tests.\r\n5. Integrate in dependency order under one owner.\r\n6. Run final full-system verification once on the combined state.\r\n\r\n### Bug investigation\r\n\r\nPotential lanes include independent reproduction, static code tracing, runtime tracing, regression history, test-gap analysis, platform-specific behavior, dependency behavior, and alternative-hypothesis verification. Keep hypotheses distinct and evidence-backed. The coordinator reconciles them and selects a supported root cause before authorizing implementation. Parallel fixes for the same suspected defect are normally redundant unless intentionally comparing isolated approaches.\r\n\r\n### Refactor\r\n\r\nStart architecture mapping, consumer inventory, and test-baseline lanes in parallel. Serialize shared-interface changes under one owner, then fan out independent package/component migrations with disjoint ownership. Integrate in dependency order and run compatibility/regression verification after all consumers move.\r\n\r\n### Frontend experience work\r\n\r\nPotential lanes include route/shell structure, navigation, bounded component groups, animation/interaction, design-system consistency, responsive behavior, accessibility, performance, browser reproduction, test coverage, visual verification, and integration review. Use up to twelve when these are genuinely independent. Assign one owner to root layout, providers, shared tokens/global styles, and route shells, plus one runtime/browser owner. Finish with an integrated responsive, keyboard, motion-mode, console, performance, and UX review against the original acceptance criteria.\r\n\r\n### Backend or database work\r\n\r\nPotential lanes include API, services, repositories, schema analysis, data integrity, security, tests, operational readiness, observability, and documentation. Separate them only where evidence or files do not overlap. Give schemas and the ordered migration chain one authoritative writer and one database/migration operator. Serialize migration generation/application and shared state mutation. Integrate API/service contracts before final database, security, regression, and deployment-readiness validation.\r\n\r\n### Documentation task\r\n\r\nPotential lanes include source inventory, contradiction review, terminology, factual verification, structural review, instruction-discovery validation, configuration validation, and editorial integration. Fan out read-only discovery and fact-checking by topic. Topic-specific drafting may run in parallel only with disjoint document ownership. Use one editorial integration owner for shared documents, terminology, links, and final formatting. Verify claims against sources and run proportionate diff/format/link checks. Do not create extra helper documents when the requested output is fixed.\r\n\r\n### Homogeneous batch investigations\r\n\r\nWhen the installed client exposes `spawn_agents_on_csv` or a verified equivalent, optional batch fan-out may handle many independent items with the same analysis: one component, route, package, animation system, test failure, migration target, document, or incident per row. Treat this capability as client-surface dependent and experimental; use ordinary named lanes when clearer.\r\n\r\nEach batch requires a stable item ID, explicit input columns, fixed output schema, scope and non-scope, evidence fields, confidence, exactly one result per worker, bounded runtime, maximum safe concurrency, consolidated output, coordinator reconciliation, and retained error rows. Never silently drop failures or assume a batch tool exists without verifying the current client.\r\n\r\n## Anti-patterns\r\n\r\nDo not:\r\n\r\n- process independent areas sequentially without a concrete reason;\r\n- leave useful worker slots idle while ready meaningful work exists;\r\n- wait for an entire worker wave when one slot becomes available;\r\n- wait for every discovery lane before starting implementation that has sufficient verified inputs;\r\n- wait for every implementation lane before integrating completed independent work when incremental integration is safe;\r\n- require every worker to finish before reviewing completed high-priority output;\r\n- spawn agents with substantially identical scopes;\r\n- make every agent scan the entire repository;\r\n- make every worker rediscover repository structure instead of reusing a shared census;\r\n- delay safe read-only fan-out until every planning field is complete;\r\n- write oversized plans or status reports whose coordination cost exceeds their practical value;\r\n- perform delegable work in the coordinator merely because delegation requires a briefing;\r\n- launch work before evidence, path, and resource ownership are defined;\r\n- launch a write-enabled worker against an unresolved, inferred, shorthand, or otherwise unverified path;\r\n- treat a nonexistent path as writable without explicitly confirming and labeling intentional new-file ownership;\r\n- allow multiple agents to edit the same file concurrently;\r\n- let multiple development servers compete for port `3000`;\r\n- make every lane run the entire test suite;\r\n- rerun expensive global checks after every small lane instead of using focused checks and one integrated gate;\r\n- use agent count as a quality metric or create microscopic artificial lanes;\r\n- maintain redundant lanes after sufficient evidence exists;\r\n- ignore slower-lane results because faster lanes finished first;\r\n- combine reports without reconciling duplicates, severity, or contradictions;\r\n- let subagents reinterpret or broaden user requirements;\r\n- use parallelism to bypass safety, review, authorization, or validation;\r\n- restart completed work after one lane fails;\r\n- claim completion before integration and verification;\r\n- create alternate application copies, port-specific versions, or abandoned variants;\r\n- use generated snapshots or obsolete/source-history trees because they are easier to discover;\r\n- hide uncertainty, partial failure, skipped validation, or incomplete integration;\r\n- let workers independently fetch/rebase/merge/commit/push or run chat/document synchronization without explicit exclusive ownership; or\r\n- stage the whole repository by default in a dirty worktree.\r\n\r\n## Adaptive plan behavior\r\n\r\nUpdate the plan when:\r\n\r\n- new dependencies or shared resources are discovered;\r\n- two lanes overlap or shared-file conflict becomes likely;\r\n- a lane becomes unnecessary or duplicates another;\r\n- supposedly independent work is found to be dependent;\r\n- a blocked lane can be narrowed or split;\r\n- a slow or broad lane can be split or reassigned to shorten the critical path without losing useful work;\r\n- additional safe parallelism becomes available;\r\n- runtime evidence contradicts static analysis;\r\n- the canonical implementation differs from the initial assumption;\r\n- a write-lane path is verified, found nonexistent, confirmed as an intentional new file, or remains unresolved;\r\n- validation reveals a pre-existing failure or regression; or\r\n- risk, completion criteria, or user authority changes.\r\n\r\nWhen adapting:\r\n\r\n1. preserve completed work and useful partial evidence;\r\n2. update dependency edges, ownership, locks, status, risk, and validation;\r\n3. notify affected lanes and stop conflicting writers before reassignment;\r\n4. record the material discovery or decision;\r\n5. start newly ready independent work promptly;\r\n6. review and integrate completed high-priority output without waiting for unrelated lanes; and\r\n7. avoid unnecessary restarts.\r\n\r\nThe plan serves the task. It may evolve, but it may never override the user's instructions or governing product requirements. Codex must move as quickly as possible without becoming careless: progressive planning, specialization, early risk resolution, incremental integration, focused validation, and prompt worker reuse exist to deliver a correct and complete result in the least practical elapsed time.\r\n", "type": "input_text"}]

It is the work that prevents every later phase from becoming archaeology.\r\n7.3 In scope\r\n• repository and package boundaries;\r\n• shared UI and domain extraction where needed;\r\n• Vision W aypoint entities and lifecycle;\r\n• immutable version model;\r\n• database migrations;\r\n• API and event contracts;\r\n• platform-adapter interface;\r\n• mock Companion adapter;\r\n• mock verification adapter;\r\n• desktop shell bootstrap;\r\n• PW A manifest and service-worker foundation;\r\n13\r\n\r\n--- PDF PAGE 31 ---\r\nVISION WAYPOINT PHASE B IMPLEMENTATION ROADMAP v1.0\r\n• feature flags;\r\n• test fixtures and contract tests;\r\n• package and protocol versioning;\r\n• governing-document placement and ADR process;\r\n• baseline observability and audit events.\r\n7.4 Out of scope\r\n• real game-window capture;\r\n• real computer-vision inference;\r\n• complete authoring wizard;\r\n• automatic waypoint builds;\r\n• automatic story progression from real evidence;\r\n• public installers or signed releases;\r\n• live AR effects.\r\nMocks are authorized only at the capture and vision-result boundaries. Domain persistence, lifecycle, versioning, story\r\nevents, and cross-shell rendering MUST be real.\r\n7.5 B‐1 work package 1: Repository and shared‐package architecture\r\n7.5.1 Objective\r\nSeparate shared product capabilities from platform shells without destabilizing the existing working website.\r\n7.5.2 Required actions\r\n1. inventory current Player, Captain, Studio, story, authentication, asset, and routing code;\r\n2. identify components that are already reusable and components tightly coupled to browser globals;\r\n3. define canonical package boundaries;\r\n4. extract shared domain and UI code incrementally;\r\n5. add dependency rules preventing shared packages from importing desktop-only or server-only code;\r\n6. preserve existing routes and user-facing behavior;\r\n7. create import aliases and lint rules to keep boundaries enforceable;\r\n8. document the package ownership and allowed dependency direction.\r\n7.5.3 Required dependency direction\r\nUI components\r\n-> domain interfaces\r\n-> service contracts\r\n-> platform adapter interfaces\r\nWeb shell\r\n-> shared UI and web adapters\r\nDesktop shell\r\n-> shared UI and desktop adapters\r\nNative services\r\n-> protocol schemas, not frontend implementation\r\n14\r\n\r\n--- PDF PAGE 32 ---\r\nVISION WAYPOINT PHASE B IMPLEMENTATION ROADMAP v1.0\r\nShared packages MUST NOT import from apps/web or apps/desktop. Platform shells may import shared packages.\r\n7.5.4 Expected deliverables\r\n• repository architecture document;\r\n• package dependency diagram;\r\n• lint or build checks for invalid imports;\r\n• shared application bootstrap;\r\n• migration plan for remaining legacy code;\r\n• tests proving both shells render the same core routes.\r\n7.6 B‐1 work package 2: Vision Waypoint domain model\r\n7.6.1 Required entities\r\nThe persistence and domain layer MUST support at least:\r\n• VisionWaypoint - stable identity and reusable library item;\r\n• VisionWaypointVersion - immutable published build lineage and editable draft state;\r\n• WaypointReferenceRecording - target, accepted-area, boundary, environmental, or diagnostic recording;\r\n• WaypointNegativeRecording - hard-negative recording and confuser classification;\r\n• WaypointStableRegion - creator-confirmed important or ignored regions across reference frames;\r\n• WaypointAcceptedPoseRegion - accepted and excluded camera regions and orientation rules;\r\n• WaypointBuildJob - queued, active, completed, canceled, or failed build;\r\n• WaypointBuildArtifact - generated runtime package components and checksums;\r\n• WaypointCalibrationReport - thresholds, distributions, datasets, engine versions, and release grade;\r\n• WaypointTestRun - positive, negative, boundary, environmental, or shadow test;\r\n• WaypointVerificationProfile - Balanced, Strict, Story-Critical, or Custom requirements;\r\n• WaypointVerificationAttempt - runtime attempt, outcome, failed gates, and story context;\r\n• WaypointEvidenceBundle - temporary or retained diagnostic metadata;\r\n• WaypointPublication - publication scope, package version, and compatibility;\r\n• WaypointUsageReference - T all T ales, blocks, drafts, or published stories using the version;\r\n• CompanionDevice - paired local device identity and capabilities;\r\n• CompanionPairingSession - short-lived pairing authorization.\r\n7.6.2 Identity rules\r\n• A waypoint has a stable ID independent of its name.\r\n• A waypoint version has its own immutable ID.\r\n• Recordings and tests are attached to a specific draft version.\r\n• A published story references a specific published waypoint version.\r\n• Renaming a waypoint does not change its identity.\r\n• Deleting a draft cannot invalidate a published story.\r\n• Archived waypoints remain resolvable when referenced by history.\r\n7.6.3 Version rules\r\nA waypoint SHALL support:\r\nStable Waypoint\r\nVersion 1 - Published\r\n15\r\n\r\n--- PDF PAGE 33 ---\r\nVISION WAYPOINT PHASE B IMPLEMENTATION ROADMAP v1.0\r\nVersion 2 - Published\r\nVersion 3 - Current Draft\r\nOnly the current draft may be edited. Publishing freezes:\r\n• runtime package checksum;\r\n• calibration report;\r\n• engine and model versions;\r\n• verification profile;\r\n• accepted pose region;\r\n• stable-region definitions;\r\n• test evidence;\r\n• compatibility metadata.\r\nA published version may be deprecated but not silently changed.\r\n7.7 B‐1 work package 3: Lifecycle and state machines\r\n7.7.1 Authoring lifecycle\r\nDRAFT\r\n-> COLLECTING_REFERENCE_DATA\r\n-> READY_TO_BUILD\r\n-> BUILDING\r\n-> NEEDS_ADDITIONAL_DATA | BUILD_FAILED | READY_FOR_TESTING\r\n-> TESTING\r\n-> UNSAFE | SHADOW_READY\r\n-> CAPTAIN_CONFIRMED\r\n-> AUTOMATIC_READY\r\n-> PUBLISHED\r\n-> DEPRECATED | OUTDATED\r\n7.7.2 State‐transition requirements\r\n• transitions MUST be explicit commands, not inferred from unrelated field values;\r\n• invalid transitions MUST fail with a domain error;\r\n• every transition MUST create an audit event;\r\n• build and publication operations MUST be idempotent;\r\n• the system MUST distinguish temporary operational failure from a product-safety failure;\r\n• UNSAFE means one or more negative cases were accepted or an equivalent critical reliability failure occurred;\r\n• OUTDATED means compatibility metadata indicates the package requires retesting or rebuilding;\r\n• rollback MUST restore the previous stable state without mutating historical evidence.\r\n7.7.3 Story‐use lifecycle\r\nA story block referencing a waypoint version may be:\r\nUNCONFIGURED\r\nCONFIGURED\r\nPACKAGE_REQUIRED\r\nPACKAGE_READY\r\nACTIVE\r\nSCANNING\r\n16\r\n\r\n--- PDF PAGE 34 ---\r\nVISION WAYPOINT PHASE B IMPLEMENTATION ROADMAP v1.0\r\nVERIFIED\r\nRETRY_REQUIRED\r\nCAPTAIN_OVERRIDE\r\nCOMPLETED\r\nThe story state and waypoint-authoring state are separate. A published waypoint may be reused by many active story\r\nsessions.\r\n7.8 B‐1 work package 4: Database migrations and persistence services\r\n7.8.1 Requirements\r\n• use the project’s canonical It should appear to perceive the journey , recognize meaningful places and objects,\r\nand reveal a hidden narrative layer at exactly the right moment.\r\nThe creator should feel as though they are using a polished game editor . Creating a visually\r\nverified story event should be comparable to creating a checkpoint, adding a cinematic, or\r\nplacing a trigger in a modern level editor . It must not feel like training a machine-learning\r\nmodel.\r\n2.2 Primary objectives\r\nThe system MUST:\r\n• enable automatic verification of story-critical game locations and visual conditions;\r\n• minimize false positives strongly enough that a wrong location does not prematurely\r\ntrigger a reveal;\r\n• avoid exact-view brittleness by supporting reasonable variation in player position, angle,\r\ndistance, field of view , resolution, lighting, weather , and graphical settings;\r\n• guide legitimate players toward successful verification instead of returning generic fail-\r\nures;\r\n• allow nontechnical creators to author , test, reuse, version, and share Vision Waypoints\r\nin the Studio;\r\n• keep the Sea of Thieves process untouched;\r\n• perform runtime processing locally by default;\r\n• attach verification results to a general event-driven story engine rather than hard-code\r\ncinematics into the verifier;\r\n• preserve Captain oversight and manual recovery;\r\n• allow gradual promotion from development to shadow mode, Captain-confirmed mode,\r\nand fully automatic progression;\r\n• support future live external-AR effects without requiring the core authoring system to\r\nbe rebuilt.\r\n2\r\n\r\n--- PDF PAGE 15 ---\r\nVISION WAYPOINT & EXTERNAL AR GOVERNING SPECIFICATION v1.0\r\n2.3 Quality hierarchy\r\nWhen tradeoffs occur , the governing priority is:\r\n1. prevent false story progression;\r\n2. preserve player trust and privacy;\r\n3. provide a successful guided retry for legitimate players;\r\n4. keep creator authoring simple;\r\n5. maintain explainability and diagnostics;\r\n6. optimize performance;\r\n7. add spectacle.\r\nA beautiful ten-second reveal is valuable. A beautiful ten-second reveal triggered by the\r\nwrong palm tree is accidental comedy and therefore not a release criterion.\r\n3\r\n\r\n--- PDF PAGE 16 ---\r\nChapter 3\r\nGoverning Principles\r\n3.1 The verifier proves; it does not guess\r\nThe system MUST use mandatory evidence gates. A high score from one stage cannot\r\ncompensate for a failed geometric, pose, negative-margin, or temporal gate.\r\n3.2 Current story context narrows the problem\r\nThe system MUST inspect only the currently active waypoint and its explicit confusers. It\r\nis not required to classify the entire Sea of Thieves world continuously .\r\n3.3 Multi‐frame evidence is the default\r\nPhase B MUST use a short guided scan, not a single screenshot. Multiple frames provide\r\nview diversity , obstruction recovery , motion evidence, and sequence consistency .\r\n3.4 Geometry outranks appearance\r\nGlobal similarity may retrieve candidates, but geometric evidence and camera localization\r\nMUST determine whether the physical scene is consistent with the target.\r\n3.5 Hard negatives are first‐class data\r\nCreators MUST record similar wrong places for high-reliability waypoints. The system\r\nMUST compare target confidence against known confusers and refuse close ties.\r\n3.6 Ambiguity is a valid result\r\nThe internal outcome set is:\r\n• VERIFIED;\r\n• INSUFFICIENT_VISUAL_EVIDENCE;\r\n• NOT_AT_TARGET.\r\n4\r\n\r\n--- PDF PAGE 17 ---\r\nVISION WAYPOINT & EXTERNAL AR GOVERNING SPECIFICATION v1.0\r\nThe verifier MUST NOT force every attempt into success or failure when the evidence is\r\nambiguous.\r\n3.7 Story logic is separate from recognition logic\r\nA Vision Waypoint proves a condition. The story graph decides what happens next. The\r\nsame waypoint may trigger different outcomes in different Tall Tales.\r\n3.8 The creator sees guidance, not computer‐vision jargon\r\nThe default Studio experience MUST use language such as “record more of the right side,”\r\n“capture another similar rock,” and “move farther away .” Raw model thresholds belong in\r\nengineering diagnostics.\r\n3.9 Published behavior is versioned\r\nA published Tall Tale MUST reference an immutable waypoint version. Updating a library\r\nwaypoint MUST NOT silently alter a published story .\r\n3.10 Safety boundaries are architectural, not optional settings\r\nThe Companion MUST NOT inject into the game, read process memory , alter game files,\r\nsimulate input, or render an in-game overlay . Codex\r\nCodex MUST preserve the following truths:\r\n1. Build a reusable Studio tool, not one-off waypoint code.\r\n2. Vision Waypoints are first-class, versioned assets.\r\n3. The default creator workflow is guided and nontechnical.\r\n4. The player performs a short multi-frame scan, not a one-frame classification.\r\n5. Current story context narrows the search but is not proof.\r\n6. Global similarity retrieves candidates; it does not unlock the story .\r\n7. Known similar wrong places are explicitly recorded and compared.\r\n8. Local geometry and 3D camera pose are central to viewpoint tolerance and false-\r\npositive prevention.\r\n9. Evidence must be spatially distributed and temporally consistent.\r\n10. Ambiguity produces no reveal.\r\n11. Guided retry protects legitimate players from brittle false negatives.\r\n12. Mandatory gates cannot be replaced by a weighted confidence average.\r\n13. The verifier emits an event; the story engine controls presentation and progression.\r\n14. Captain override, shadow mode, truth labeling, and demotion are required.\r\n15. Runtime is local-first, visible, private, and nonretaining by default.\r\n16. The game process remains untouched; no injection, memory reading, file modification,\r\nautomation, or in-game overlay .\r\n17. Published waypoint versions are immutable and test-certified.\r\n18. Unsafe waypoints cannot publish for automatic progression.\r\n19. Future live external AR uses the same verification assets and event contracts.\r\n20. Any architectural departure requires an ADR rather than a creative surprise hidden in\r\na commit.\r\nFinal Governing Statement\r\nThe product succeeds when a creator can say , “The player must stand near this\r\nrock and look at it before the hidden message appears,” and the Studio handles cap-\r\nture, mapping, confusers, calibration, testing, packaging, runtime proof, guided retry ,\r\nand cinematic triggering without requiring code. - Shared Next.js UI is packaged by Electron and exposed as a PWA; there is no duplicated frontend tree.
- Service-worker policy is static-shell only and network-only for APIs/authenticated surfaces.
- Electron bridge is narrow: `vision.getCapabilities`, `vision.prepareMockScan`, and `app.getDiagnostics`.

Historical transcript evidence shows:

- Full validation exit `0`
- 33 Vitest files / 102 tests passed
- 2 Electron bridge tests passed
- 24 Playwright passed / 8 WebKit mutation tests skipped
- clean six-migration SQLite bootstrap
- production build/restart passed
- desktop build/smoke passed
- unsigned installer hash recorded

This was not independently rerun during this audit.

### Contradictions and material gaps

1. **Exact-once proof is incomplete.**

   The duplicate E2E replays the same idempotency key internally and proves one `verificationSatisfied` event. It does not test distinct-key or concurrent submissions against the same request, altered-payload reuse of an existing idempotency key, or automatic/Captain races. `submitVerification` checks request status before its transaction and does not recheck it transactionally; multiple distinct accepted events remain possible even though `completeBlock` suppresses a second block completion.

2. **Database immutability/reference constraints are incomplete.**

   Services prevent published edits and reject draft bindings, but the database does not constrain `StoryWaypointBinding.waypointVersionId` to a published version, does not ensure `waypointId` matches the referenced version’s waypoint, and has no published-row update trigger. The roadmap explicitly asked migration constraints to prevent published stories referencing editable drafts.

3. **Publication is not idempotent.**

   Repeating `publishDraftVersion` throws `PUBLISHED_VERSION_IMMUTABLE`; the roadmap requires build/publication operations to be idempotent.

4. **Two incompatible `VisionCapabilities` contracts exist.**

   `src/vision/protocol.ts` defines governed capabilities such as `nativeCapture`, `globalHotkeys`, and `localInference`; `src/vision/platform-adapters.ts` independently defines a different `VisionCapabilities` shape using `capture`, `deterministicMock`, and `platform`. This violates the single-authoritative-contract goal.

5. **Feature flags are mostly declarative.**

   Only selected APIs/progression use flags. `publicVisionFeatureFlags` is unused; Studio always shows the Vision link, PWA registration is always mounted, adapter selection ignores flags/capabilities, and most future flags appear only in resolution/diagnostics. The requirement that disabled functionality be hidden and nonfunctional is not met.

6. **Captain interface is partial.**

   The Captain component is read-only diagnostics plus copy-summary. It lacks the required UI actions for scenario selection, start, cancel, duplicate replay, stale simulation, approve, reject, and retry. An untested approve/reject API exists; no retry action exists. The completion report’s “approve/reject/retry fallbacks” claim is unsupported.

7. **Player cancellation is partial.**

   Releasing early cancels only the local pre-attempt hold timer. Once the request starts there is no visible in-flight Cancel control, although a cancel API/adapter method exists.

8. **Desktop parity evidence is weaker than claimed.**

   The packaged smoke verifies the local shared page title. The E2E “desktop path” posts `platform: DESKTOP` directly to HTTP; it does not instantiate `DesktopPlatformAdapter`, invoke the real preload bridge from the renderer, or navigate Player/Captain/Studio in the packaged shell.

9. **PWA installability is not fully proven.**

   Tests inspect manifest/service-worker/offline policy, but no browser installability audit or actual install/launch flow was recorded. The completion report acknowledges no OS-level install ceremony.

10. **Test coverage is broad but not as comprehensive as the prompt.**

   Source-specific tests comprise 3 domain cases, 2 protocol cases, 2 adapter cases, 1 permission case, 2 flag cases, 2 PWA policy cases, 2 Electron cases, and 2 large E2E cases. Missing focused coverage includes lifecycle services, live MySQL, migration downgrade/reference constraints, disabled UI behavior, actual Desktop adapter parity, Captain actions, in-flight cancel, and concurrency/altered-duplicate behavior.

11. **Completion report format is noncompliant.**

   It never states the required `PASS`, `PASS WITH DOCUMENTED LIMITATIONS`, or `FAIL`, while claiming implementation completion despite unchecked B1 obligations. Under the governing binary exit rule, this phase is not complete.

### Current-main overlap and stale-base risk

Committed-main overlap since merge base is only four `Codex_Chats` paths; no committed B1 application source is present on main.

However, the current canonical working tree has active uncommitted overlap in five functional files:

- `eslint.config.mjs`
- `scripts/test-all.ps1`
- `src/app/layout.tsx`
- `src/components/player/journal/TallTaleJournalSession.tsx`
- `src/components/studio/StudioHome.tsx`

Those five must be ported semantically into the current canonical UI. Also avoid restoring the stale hard-coded application version `0.3.0-b1`.

### Assessment

- Implemented: substantial real foundation—persistence, migrations, versioning services, protocol, mock attempts, Studio/editor/story/Player integration, shared Electron/PWA shells, audit and historical validation.
- Partial: lifecycle enforcement, exact-once concurrency, feature gating, Captain controls, cancellation, sharing/collaboration, adapter selection/contracts, PWA/desktop proof.
- Missing: live MySQL proof, actual desktop adapter/navigation E2E, actual PWA install proof, Captain action UI/retry, transactional concurrency and altered-duplicate tests.
- Mock status: capture and inference are correctly deterministic development mocks; persistence, publication, binding, attempts, and progression are real.
- Production readiness: **No**. Useful integration foundation, not B1-exit-gate complete.
- Truthful evidence-weighted completion estimate: **approximately 72%**.
- Original B1 exit result: **FAIL / PARTIAL**, despite the completion report’s stronger language.

Recommended recovery action: preserve all five commits, integrate/extract `78ecab9` and `17f2ac0` semantically, preserve but annotate the three evidence/chat commits, exclude the chat-sync commit from application cherry-picking, consolidate capabilities/flags/contracts, and add the missing concurrency, Captain, desktop, PWA, migration, and disabled-state proofs before calling B1 complete.
